(الف) آپ نے حضرت حضرمی سے فرمایا کیا تمہارے پاس گواہ ہے؟ کہا نہیں ! آپ نے فرمایا پھر تو تمہارے لئے اس کی قسم کا حق ہے۔ دوسری روایت میں ہے آپ نے خطبے میں فرمایا گواہ مدعی پر اور قسم مدعی علیہ پر ہے۔

2740 (۲) واذا نكل المدعى عليه عن اليمين قضى عليه بالنكول والزمه ما ادعى اس کے قبضے میں چیز ہے تو قبضہ ہونا قوت کی دلیل ہے۔ کیونکہ گواہ دونوں کے پاس ہیں اور قبضہ ہونا ایک قسم کی زیادہ قوت ہونا ہے اس لئے ذی الید کے بینہ کو ترجیح ہوگی۔ اور اس کے بینہ کے مطابق چیز ذی الید کی ہوگی (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله ان رجـلـيــن تداعيا بدابة فاقام كل واحد منهما البينة انها دابته فقضى بها رسول الله الا الله الذي في يديه (الف) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب المتداعین میتا زمان شیما فی ید احدهما و يتقیم کل واحد منهما علی ذلک بیته ج عاشر ص ۴۳۳ نمبر ۲۱۲۲۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دونوں نے دعوی کیا اور مطلق ملک کا دعوی کیا اور بعینہ بھی پیش کیا تو آپ نے قبضے والے کے لئے فیصلہ کیا۔ اور اگر ملک مقید کا دعوی کرے مثلا دونوں کہے کہ یہ اونٹنی میری ملکیت ہے کیونکہ میرے یہاں پیدا ہوئی ہے تو بالا تفاق اس صورت میں ذی الید کے بینہ کو تر جیح دی جائے گی و

حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر ان رجلين اختصما الى النبى الله الله في ناقة فقال كل واحد منهما نتجت هذه الناقة عندى واقام بينة فقضى بها رسول الله الا الله الذى هى فى يديه (ب) ( سنن اليقي ، باب المتد اعیین میتاز عان شیئا في يد احدهما ويقيم كل واحد منهما علی ذلک بیته ج عاشر ص ۴۳۳ نمبر ۲۱۲۲۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ملک کے دعوی کے ساتھ یہ بھی کہا کہ یہ اونٹنی میرے یہاں پیدا ہوئی ہے اس لئے یہ میری ملکیت ہے اس لئے یہ ملک مقید کا دعوی ہوا۔ اور اس میں ذکر الید کے لئے آپ نے فیصلہ فرمایا (۲) یوں بھی جب مالک ہونے کا سبب بیان کیا تو یقین ہو گیا کہ چیز اس کی ہے اور بینہ بھی پیش کیا اور قبضہ بھی ہے اس لئے ان تینوں علامتوں کی وجہ سے قبضے والے کے لئے فیصلہ کر دیا گیا۔
140) And the evidence of the possessor is not accepted in absolute ownership.

[Commentary:] The evidence of the possessor is not accepted in absolute ownership.

Here there are three terms that we should understand first. Dhu al-yad: the person in whose possession the claimed item is, he is called dhu al-yad. Since the item is demanded from him, he is also called the defendant (mad'iy 'alayh). Kharj: the person not in possession of the claimed item, he is called kharj. Since he is demanding the item, he is also the plaintiff (mudda'i). Mulk mutlaq: a person claims 'this item is mine' but does not state the cause of his ownership – whether he bought it, was gifted it, or it was born in his house – if he does not state the cause of ownership, this is called mulk mutlaq. And if he states the cause of ownership, that is called mulk muqayyad. The scenario is that the kharj and dhu al-yad both claim that the item is theirs and they do not state the cause of ownership, rather they claim absolute ownership (mulk mutlaq). Then both produce their witnesses. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the evidence of the kharj (outsider) will be accepted and judgment will be given accordingly. Since they do not state the cause of ownership, it cannot be known which one is the owner. Therefore, the matter depends solely on evidence. The hadith has already passed that the evidence of the plaintiff (mudda'i), i.e., the kharj, is given weight. Because the possessor (dhu al-yad), i.e., the defendant, is only required to take an oath, not to produce evidence. In the hadith of Hadrami and Kindi, both claimed land and did not state the cause of how the land was theirs, i.e., they claimed absolute ownership (mulk mutlaq). So the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepted the evidence of Hadrami (the kharj) and did not accept the evidence of Kindi (the possessor), rather he required him to take an oath. The portion of the hadith is: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Hadrami: Do you have evidence? He said: No. He said: Then you have his oath.' In another narration: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) said in his sermon: Evidence is upon the plaintiff and the oath is upon the defendant.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). In this hadith, the evidence of Hadrami, who is both the kharj and the plaintiff, was accepted, and the evidence of Kindi, who is the possessor and defendant, was not accepted; rather an oath was required from him. Therefore, in our school, in absolute ownership (mulk mutlaq), the evidence of the kharj (outsider) will be given preference. Imam Shafi'i says that the evidence of the possessor (dhu al-yad) and defendant will be given preference.

[Footnote (a): The Prophet said to Hadrami: Do you have evidence? He said: No. He said: Then you have his oath. Another narration: The Prophet said in his sermon: Evidence is on the plaintiff and the oath on the defendant.]

2740 (2) And if the defendant refuses to take the oath, judgment is given against him due to refusal, and what was claimed is imposed upon him. Because the item is in his possession, possession is an indicator of strength. Since both have witnesses, and possession is a type of greater strength, therefore the evidence of the possessor is given preference, and according to his evidence, the item belongs to the possessor. In a hadith: From Jabir ibn Abdullah that two men disputed about an animal, and each produced evidence that it was his animal, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) judged it for the one in whose hands it was (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). In this hadith, both claimed and claimed absolute ownership and produced evidence, so the Prophet judged for the possessor. And if they claim restricted ownership (mulk muqayyad), for example both say 'This camel is my property because it was born in my place', then by agreement in this case the evidence of the possessor will be given preference.

In another hadith: From Jabir that two men disputed before the Prophet (peace be upon him) about a she-camel. Each said 'This she-camel was born at my place' and produced evidence. So the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) judged it for the one in whose hands it was (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). In this hadith, with the claim of ownership they also said that the camel was born at their place, so this is a claim of restricted ownership (mulk muqayyad). In that case, the Prophet judged for the possessor. Likewise, when he stated the cause of ownership, certainty was achieved that the item is his, and he also produced evidence, and he has possession, so due to these three signs, judgment was given for the possessor.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage deals with the rules of evidence (bayyinah) in claims of absolute ownership (mulk mutlaq) – where neither party states how they came to own the item. The author first defines three key terms: dhu al-yad (the possessor), kharj (the outsider/plaintiff), and mulk mutlaq (absolute ownership). The scenario: both the outsider and the possessor claim absolute ownership and each produces witnesses. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the evidence of the outsider is accepted. The reasoning: since both only make an absolute claim without specifying a cause, there is no basis to prefer one over the other except the evidence. The hadith of Hadrami and Kindi is cited as proof: the Prophet accepted the evidence of the outsider (Hadrami) and required an oath from the possessor (Kindi), not evidence. This is also supported by the general principle: "al-bayyinatu 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yaminu 'ala al-mudda'i 'alayh" (evidence is on the plaintiff, oath on the defendant). The author then contrasts the Shafi'i position: Imam Shafi'i gives preference to the evidence of the possessor, arguing that possession itself is a sign of ownership that adds weight. The Hanafi response is implicit: in mulk mutlaq, possession is not considered a stronger indicator because both claims are equally unsupported by cause. However, when the claim is mulk muqayyad (ownership with stated cause), such as "this camel was born in my home," then the Hanafis agree with Shafi'i that the possessor's evidence is preferred, as shown in the hadith of the two men and the she-camel. The passage thus clarifies the distinction: in mulk mutlaq, the outsider's evidence is accepted; in mulk muqayyad, the possessor's evidence is accepted.

Key Terms
ذو الید (dhu al-yad): The person in possession of the claimed item; also called the defendant (mad'iy 'alayh).
خارج (kharj): The person not in possession of the claimed item; also the plaintiff (mudda'i).
ملک مطلق (mulk mutlaq): A claim of ownership without stating the cause (e.g., 'this is mine' without specifying how it became one's property).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi court, in a claim of absolute ownership (mulk mutlaq), whose evidence is accepted?
A) The evidence of the possessor (dhu al-yad).
B) The evidence of the outsider (kharj).
C) Neither, the judge asks for a cause.
D) The case is dismissed.

Key Takeaway
In absolute ownership claims (mulk mutlaq), the Hanafi school accepts the evidence of the outsider, not the possessor.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute and the Distinction with Mulk Muqayyad
Explaining the dispute and the resolution via distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on evidence acceptance, explain the distinction between mulk mutlaq and mulk muqayyad, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Possession tips the scale only when ownership cause is stated; in absolute claims, evidence is the only decider.

This lesson delves into the inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on evidence in ownership claims. You will see how the Hanafi school distinguishes between absolute ownership (mulk mutlaq) and restricted ownership (mulk muqayyad) to reconcile conflicting hadiths, and understand the practical consequences for judgment.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the possessor's evidence is always preferred, because possession itself is a sign of ownership that tips the scale when both have evidence.
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof
The hadith of Jabir: two men claimed an animal, both produced evidence, and the Prophet judged for the possessor. This is cited as support.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
3
Understand the Hanafi response
Hanafis argue that the hadith of Jabir is a case of mulk muqayyad (restricted ownership) where the cause was stated, so all schools agree the possessor's evidence is preferred. The hadith of Hadrami is specific to mulk mutlaq.
4
Distinguish mulk muqayyad
When the cause of ownership is stated (e.g., 'it was born in my house'), the possessor's evidence is preferred by consensus. The Hanafi position thus harmonizes the two hadiths.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a Hanafi judge rules for the outsider in mulk mutlaq, while a Shafi'i judge rules for the possessor. This difference disappears in mulk muqayyad.

لا تقبل بينة صاحب اليد في الملك المطلق.

یہاں تین اصطلاح ہیں جن کو پہلے سمجھیں ۔ ذی الید : جس کے قبضے میں دعوی کی چیز ہو اس کو ذی الید کہتے ہیں۔ چونکہ اس سے چیز لینے کا مطالبہ ہے اس لئے اس کو مدعی علیہ کہتے ہیں۔ خارج : جس کے قبضے میں دعوی کی چیز نہ ہو اس کو خارج کہتے ہیں۔ چونکہ وہ چیز لینے کا مطالبہ کر رہا ہے اس لئے وہ مدعی بھی ہے۔ ملک مطلق : آدمی دعوی کرے کہ یہ چیز میری ہے لیکن یہ بیان نہ کرے کہ میری ملکیت کس سبب سے ہوئی ہے۔ خریدا ہے یا ہبہ کیا ہے یا اس کے گھر پیدا ہوئی ہے؟ مالک ہونے کے سبب کو بیان نہ کرے تو اس کو ملک مطلق کہتے ہیں۔ اور مالک بننے کا سبب بیان کرے تو اس کو ملک مقید کہتے ہیں۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ خارج اور ذی الید دونوں دعوی کرتے ہیں کہ یہ چیز میری ہے اور میری ہونے کا سبب بیان نہیں کرتے بلکہ ملک مطلق کا دعوی کرتے ہیں۔ پھر دونوں اپنے اپنے گواہ پیش کرتے ہیں تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک خارج کے بینہ کو مانیں گے اور اسی کے مطابق فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔ چیز کی ملکیت کا سبب بیان نہیں کرتے اس لئے کسی ایک کے ہونے کی وجہ نہیں معلوم ہوسکی۔ اس لئے اب دارو مدار صرف بینہ پر ہوگا (۲) پہلے حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ مدعی یعنی خارج کے بینہ کا اعتبار ہے۔ کیونکہ ذی السید یعنی مدعی علیہ پر تو قسم ہے نہ کہ اس پر بینہ۔ حضرت حضرمی والی حدیث میں حضرت حضرمی اور کندی دونوں نے زمین کا دعوی کیا اور زمین کس طرح ان کی ہے اس کا سبب بیان نہیں فرمایا یعنی ملک مطلق کا دعوی کیا تو آپ نے حضرت حضرمی یعنی خارج کے بینہ کا اعتبار کیا اور ذی الید یعنی کندی کے بینہ کا اعتبار نہیں کیا بلکہ ان پر قسم لازم کی ۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ فقال النبی الا الله للحضر می الک بینة؟ قال لا! قال فلک یمینه . دوسری روایت میں ہے. ان النبی الله قال في خطبته البينة على المدعى واليمين على المدعى عليه (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی ان البی یہ علی المدعی والیمین علی المدعی علیه ص ۲۴۹ نمبر ۱۳۴۱/۱۳۴۰/ ابو داؤد شریف، باب الرجل يحلف علی علمه فیما غاب عنه ص ۱۵۴ نمبر ۳۶۲۳) اس حدیث میں حضرت حضرمی جو خارج بھی ہیں اور مدعی بھی ہیں ان کے بینہ کا اعتبار کیا اور حضرت کندی جو ذی الید ہے جس کے قبضے میں زمین ہے اور مدعی علیہ ہے اس کے بینہ کا اعتبار نہیں کیا بلکہ اس پر ستم لازم کی ۔ اس لئے ہمارے یہاں ملک مطلق میں خارج کے بینہ اور گواہ کو تر جیح دی جائے گی۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ذی الید یعنی قبضہ والا اور مدعی علیہ کے بینہ کو ترجیح ہوگی۔

(الف) آپ نے حضرت حضرمی سے فرمایا کیا تمہارے پاس گواہ ہے؟ کہا نہیں ! آپ نے فرمایا پھر تو تمہارے لئے اس کی قسم کا حق ہے۔ دوسری روایت میں ہے آپ نے خطبے میں فرمایا گواہ مدعی پر اور قسم مدعی علیہ پر ہے۔

Imam Shafi'i says that the evidence of the possessor (dhu al-yad) and defendant will be given preference.

[Footnote (a): The Prophet said to Hadrami: Do you have evidence? He said: No. He said: Then you have his oath. Another narration: The Prophet said in his sermon: Evidence is on the plaintiff and the oath on the defendant.]

2740 (2) And if the defendant refuses to take the oath, judgment is given against him due to refusal, and what was claimed is imposed upon him. Because the item is in his possession, possession is an indicator of strength. Since both have witnesses, and possession is a type of greater strength, therefore the evidence of the possessor is given preference, and according to his evidence, the item belongs to the possessor. In a hadith: From Jabir ibn Abdullah that two men disputed about an animal, and each produced evidence that it was his animal, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) judged it for the one in whose hands it was (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). In this hadith, both claimed and claimed absolute ownership and produced evidence, so the Prophet judged for the possessor. And if they claim restricted ownership (mulk muqayyad), for example both say 'This camel is my property because it was born in my place', then by agreement in this case the evidence of the possessor will be given preference.

In another hadith: From Jabir that two men disputed before the Prophet (peace be upon him) about a she-camel. Each said 'This she-camel was born at my place' and produced evidence. So the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) judged it for the one in whose hands it was (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). In this hadith, with the claim of ownership they also said that the camel was born at their place, so this is a claim of restricted ownership (mulk muqayyad). In that case, the Prophet judged for the possessor. Likewise, when he stated the cause of ownership, certainty was achieved that the item is his, and he also produced evidence, and he has possession, so due to these three signs, judgment was given for the possessor.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage deals with the rules of evidence (bayyinah) in claims of absolute ownership (mulk mutlaq) – where neither party states how they came to own the item. The author first defines three key terms: dhu al-yad (the possessor), kharj (the outsider/plaintiff), and mulk mutlaq (absolute ownership). The scenario: both the outsider and the possessor claim absolute ownership and each produces witnesses. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the evidence of the outsider is accepted. The reasoning: since both only make an absolute claim without specifying a cause, there is no basis to prefer one over the other except the evidence. The hadith of Hadrami and Kindi is cited as proof: the Prophet accepted the evidence of the outsider (Hadrami) and required an oath from the possessor (Kindi), not evidence. This is also supported by the general principle: "al-bayyinatu 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yaminu 'ala al-mudda'i 'alayh" (evidence is on the plaintiff, oath on the defendant). The author then contrasts the Shafi'i position: Imam Shafi'i gives preference to the evidence of the possessor, arguing that possession itself is a sign of ownership that adds weight. The Hanafi response is implicit: in mulk mutlaq, possession is not considered a stronger indicator because both claims are equally unsupported by cause. However, when the claim is mulk muqayyad (ownership with stated cause), such as "this camel was born in my home," then the Hanafis agree with Shafi'i that the possessor's evidence is preferred, as shown in the hadith of the two men and the she-camel. The passage thus clarifies the distinction: in mulk mutlaq, the outsider's evidence is accepted; in mulk muqayyad, the possessor's evidence is accepted.

Key Terms
ملک مقید (mulk muqayyad): A claim of ownership with specification of the cause (e.g., 'I bought it' or 'it was born in my home').
خارج (kharj): The person not in possession of the claimed item; also the plaintiff (mudda'i).
ملک مطلق (mulk mutlaq): A claim of ownership without stating the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi court, what is the ruling when both parties claim ownership with a stated cause (mulk muqayyad) and both produce evidence?
A) The outsider's evidence is accepted.
B) The possessor's evidence is accepted.
C) The case is decided by casting lots.
D) The judge asks for further evidence.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on evidence is resolved by distinguishing between absolute ownership (outsider's evidence) and restricted ownership (possessor's evidence).

Ruling on Defendant's Refusal to Take Oath (Nukul)
Stating that refusal to take an oath leads to judgment against the defendant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a defendant refuses to take the oath (nukul) and explain why the judge rules against him without requiring the plaintiff to swear.

Core Idea
Refusal to take the oath (nukul) is equivalent to losing the case – the judge rules against the defendant.

In Islamic legal procedure, when a plaintiff has no evidence, he may demand that the defendant take an oath denying the claim. If the defendant refuses, the judge must rule against him. This passage explains the ruling and its rationale, emphasizing that the plaintiff does not need to swear an oath after the defendant's refusal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the plaintiff has no witnesses, so he requests the defendant to take an oath. This is the context for nukul.
2
Understand defendant's refusal (nukul)
Nukul is the defendant's refusal to take the oath after being lawfully requested. It can be explicit or implicit (e.g., silence).
3
State the ruling
The judge rules against the defendant and imposes the claimed obligation on him. The plaintiff is not required to take an oath.
4
Analyze the rationale
The oath is the defendant's obligation (al-yaminu 'ala al-mudda'i 'alayh). By refusing, he fails his duty, and the claim stands against him.
Proof from hadith: 'Evidence is on the plaintiff, oath on the defendant.'
5
Consider the defendant's possible motives
The defendant may either be benevolently giving the item (bazl) or tacitly admitting the claim. Both lead to the same ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
2741 (۲) واذا نكل المدعى عليه عن اليمين قضى عليه بالنكول والزمه ما ادعى

مدعی کے پاس گواہ نہیں تھے اس لئے اس نے مدعی علیہ کو تم کھانے کے لئے کہا لیکن مدعی علیہ نے بھی قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو اس کے انکار کے بعد قاضی فیصلہ کر دے گا کہ یہ چیز مدعی کی ہے۔ اب دوبارہ مدعی سے قسم نہیں کھلائی جائے گی۔ پہلے حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ مدعی سے تم نہیں لی جائے گی۔ اس پر تو گواہ ہے تم نہیں ہے اس لئے اس سے قسم نہیں لی جائے گی۔ اور مدعی علیہ نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا تو اس کے دو مطالب ہیں۔ ایک مطلب تو یہ ہے کہ یہ چیز تو میری ہی ہے لیکن اللہ کے محترم نام کے ساتھ میں قسم نہیں کھانا چاہتا۔ چلو یہ مدعی کو دے دیتا ہوں ایسا کرنے کو بازل کہتے ہیں۔ یعنی میں نے مدعی پر اپنی چیز خرچ کر دی۔ اور دوسرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ دبے زبان اقرار کرتا ہوں کہ یہ چیز حقیقت میں مدعی کی ہی ہے اس لئے قسم نہیں کھاتا۔ تا ہم دونوں صورتوں میں مدعی علیہ نے مدعی کو چیز دینے کی رضامندی ظاہر کر دی ہے اس لئے قسم سے انکار کیا اس لئے مدعی کے حق میں فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت
2741 (2) And if the defendant refuses to take the oath, judgment is given against him due to refusal, and what was claimed is imposed upon him.

The plaintiff did not have witnesses, so he asked the defendant to take an oath, but the defendant also refused to take the oath. Then after his refusal, the judge will decide that the item belongs to the plaintiff. Now, the plaintiff will not be asked to take an oath again. The hadith has already passed that the plaintiff will not be made to take an oath. He has evidence, not an oath. So an oath will not be taken from him. And when the defendant refused to take the oath, there are two possible motives: one meaning is that the item is indeed mine, but I do not want to swear by the honorable name of Allah. Let me give it to the plaintiff – this is called 'bazl' (spending), i.e., I have spent my property on the plaintiff. The other meaning is that I silently admit that the item is actually the plaintiff's, so I do not take an oath. In both cases, the defendant has expressed willingness to give the item to the plaintiff, so he refused the oath. Therefore, judgment will be given in favor of the plaintiff. (2) The proof of this is in the hadith.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when the defendant (mad'iy 'alayh) refuses to take the oath (nukul). The scenario: the plaintiff has no witnesses, so he requests the defendant to take an oath (that the claim is false). If the defendant refuses, the judge rules against him and declares the claimed item as belonging to the plaintiff. The author clarifies that the plaintiff is not required to take an oath, because the burden of proof is on the plaintiff (he should have evidence) and the oath is on the defendant. Since the defendant refused, the judge treats this refusal as either a gesture of generosity (bazl – the defendant chooses to give the item to avoid swearing) or a tacit admission. In both interpretations, the result is the same: the judge rules in favor of the plaintiff. The proof is implied from the general principles of evidence and oath, and from the hadith cited earlier (the principle that evidence is on the plaintiff, oath on the defendant). The refusal of the defendant to take the oath shifts the case in favor of the plaintiff.

Key Terms
نكول (nukul): Refusal of the defendant to take the oath after being requested by the plaintiff who has no evidence.
بازل (bazl): Spending or giving away one's property; here it means the defendant voluntarily gives the claimed item to the plaintiff to avoid swearing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the defendant refuses to take the oath in a case where the plaintiff has no witnesses, what is the ruling?
A) The defendant is imprisoned until he takes the oath.
B) The judge rules in favor of the plaintiff without requiring the plaintiff to take an oath.
C) The plaintiff must produce a witness or lose the case.
D) The case is postponed indefinitely.

Key Takeaway
Refusal to take the oath (nukul) results in a judgment against the defendant, as he has failed in his procedural duty.

Ruling on Defendant's Refusal to Swear (Nukul) and Judge's Warning
Explains the ruling when defendant refuses oath and the judge's three-time warning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nukul and explain why the plaintiff does not need to swear after the defendant's refusal.

Core Idea
Nukul (defendant's refusal to swear) substitutes for a witness, leading to immediate judgment against the defendant.

In Hanafi judicial procedure, when the plaintiff lacks witnesses, he may demand an oath from the defendant. But what happens if the defendant refuses to swear? This passage from the classical fiqh text clarifies the ruling on nukul (refusal) and the judge's procedural caution to warn the defendant three times. The discussion also presents the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who requires the plaintiff to swear after nukul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
Read the passage to determine the act being ruled upon (defendant's refusal to swear) and the immediate legal consequence (judgment against the defendant). Note that the plaintiff has no witnesses.
The passage begins with a discussion of possession and witnesses, then transitions to nukul.
2
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
Find the hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb quoted in the passage. Identify that it directly equates nukul to a second witness.
Exact words: 'فنكوله بمنزلة شاهد آخر'
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the phrase 'بمنزلة شاهد آخر' proves that nukul alone is sufficient for judgment without requiring the plaintiff to swear. The nukul fills the gap of the missing second witness.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut (single narration) but its meaning is clear.
4
Understand the inter-madhhab conflict
Identify the Shafi'i position: the plaintiff must swear after nukul. Note their proof (athar from 'Ali) and the Hanafi response that the athar applies to a different scenario (plaintiff with witness, not nukul).
The dispute highlights the Hanafi principle that nukul is stronger than a single witness.
5
Examine the procedural recommendation
Note the judge's optional but recommended practice of warning the defendant three times before ruling. Understand that a single refusal is sufficient but the triple warning is for caution and fairness.
This is a sunnah practice, not wajib.

الحلف مع البیته ج عا شرص ۴۴۱ نمبر ۲۱۲۴۸) اس اثر کی وجہ سے مدعی پر ختم ہوگی۔ النکول : قسم کھانے سے انکار کرنا۔ ۲۷۴۲) (۱۳) قاضی کے لئے مناسب ہے کہ اس سے کہے کہ میں تم پر قسم تین بار پیش کرتا ہوں ، پس اگر تم نے قسم کھالی تو ٹھیک ہے ورنہ تمہارے خلاف فیصلہ کروں گا اس نے مطابق جس کا مدعی دعوی کرتا ہے۔ تفریق ایک مرتبہ بھی قاضی مدعی علیہ پر قسم پیش کر دے اور وہ قسم کھانے سے انکار کرے تو قاضی کے لئے گنجائش ہے کہ وہ مدعی علیہ کے خلاف فیصلہ کر دے۔ کیونکہ اوپر کی احادیث میں ایک مرتبہ کے انکار سے فیصلہ کا اشارہ ملتا ہے۔ لیکن چونکہ مدعی علیہ کے سامنے معاملہ نہیں ہے اور ہو سکتا ہے کہ قانون سے واقف نہ ہو اس لئے بہتر ہے کہ قاضی پہلے سے آگاہ کر دے کہ میں تم پر تین مرتبہ قسم پیش کروں گا۔ اگر تم نے قسم کھالی تو تمہارے موافق فیصلہ ہوگا کیونکہ مدعی کے پاس گواہ نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر تم نے تینوں مرتبہ قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا تو تمہارے خلاف فیصلہ کروں گا جس کا دعوی مدعی کر رہا ہے۔ ... ممکن ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کوقانون کا پتا نہ ہوکر سے انکار کے بعد میرے خلاف فیصلہ ہو جائے گا اس لئے اس کو پہلے سے بتادے کہ تین مرتبہ قسم پیش کروں گا۔ اور قسم سے انکار کے بعد تمہارے خلاف فیصلہ ہوگا۔ اور تین مرتبہ احتیاط کے لئے ہے ورنہ ایک مرتبہ قسم پیش کر دے اور وہ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا اگر عورت شوہر کی طلاق کا دعوی کرے اور اس پر ایک عادل گواہ لائے تو اس کے شوہر کو قسم کھلائی جائے گی ، پس اگر اس نے قسم کھائی تو گواہ کی گواہی باطل ہو جائے گی اور اگر انکار کر دیا تو اس کا انکار دوسرے گواہ کے درجے میں ہوگا اور عورت پر طلاق جائز ہو جائے گی (ب) حضرت علی گواہ کے ساتھ مدعی کی قسم بھی ضروری سمجھتے تھے .
2741 (2) And if the defendant refuses the oath, judgment is passed against him due to nukul, and he is compelled to what was claimed. If there is a thing in his possession, possession is evidence of strength. Because both have witnesses and possession is a type of greater strength, so the witness of the possessor is given preference. And according to his witness, the thing belongs to the possessor. (2) There is a hadith. From Jabir ibn Abdullah: Two men disputed about an animal and each brought evidence that it was his animal, so the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, judged it for the one in whose hand it was. (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on two disputants...). This hadith says that both claimed absolute ownership and brought proof, so he judged for the possessor. And if they claim restricted ownership, e.g., both say 'This she-camel is mine because it was born at my place', then by agreement in this case the witness of the possessor is given preference. And there is a hadith: From Jabir that two men disputed before the Prophet about a she-camel, and each said 'This she-camel was born at my place' and brought evidence, so the Messenger of Allah judged it for the one in whose hand it was. (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi...). This hadith says that along with the claim of ownership, they also said that the she-camel was born at their place, so it was a claim of restricted ownership. And in it, the Prophet judged for the possessor. (2) Also, when he stated the reason for ownership, it became certain that the thing is his, and he brought evidence and he has possession, so due to these three signs, judgment was given for the possessor. [2741] (12) If the defendant refuses the oath, judgment is passed against him due to his refusal, and he is compelled to what was claimed. The plaintiff had no witnesses, so he asked the defendant to swear, but the defendant also refused to swear, so after his refusal the judge will judge that the thing belongs to the plaintiff. Now the plaintiff will not be made to swear again. A hadith has passed that the plaintiff will not be made to swear. He has a witness, he does not have an oath, so he is not made to swear. And when the defendant refused to swear, there are two implications. One meaning is that the thing is mine, but I do not wish to swear by the honorable name of Allah. Let me give it to the plaintiff; this is called bazl (giving voluntary gift). That is, I spend my thing on the plaintiff. The second meaning is that with a low tongue he admits that the thing truly belongs to the plaintiff, so he does not swear. Nevertheless, in both cases, the defendant has shown willingness to give the thing to the plaintiff, so he refused the oath, so judgment will be given in favor of the plaintiff. (2) There is proof of this in a hadith. Footnote: (a) Jabir said: Two men disputed about an animal, each brought evidence that it was his animal, so he judged it for the one in whose hand it was. (b) Jabir narrated: Two men came to the Presence disputing about a she-camel. Both said that this she-camel was born at their place and brought witnesses, so he judged it for the one in whose hand it was. 2742) It is appropriate for the judge to say to him: I present the oath to you three times. If you swear, then [fine], otherwise I will judge against you according to what he claimed. There is a hadith from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: He said: When a woman claims divorce from her husband and brings one upright witness for that, then her husband is made to swear. If he swears, the witness's testimony is nullified; and if he refuses, his refusal is in the position of another witness, and her divorce becomes valid. (a) (Ibn Majah...). This hadith says that refusal to swear is in the position of a second witness and judgment is passed accordingly. Imam al-Shafi'i says: When the defendant refuses the oath, judgment is not passed; rather, the plaintiff is made to swear. He will swear that the thing is mine, then judgment will be passed for the plaintiff. There is an athar that when the plaintiff brings evidence, still the plaintiff is made to swear and then judgment is passed. When he brings a witness, they give the oath to the plaintiff. Here the defendant refused the oath, so more doubt arises. So by analogy, it is even more appropriate that the plaintiff is made to swear to ensure full clarity that the thing belongs to the plaintiff. (2) The athar is: 'Ali used to require the oath along with the evidence. (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi...). Because of this athar, the matter ends with the plaintiff. Nukul: refusal to swear. 2742 (13) It is appropriate for the judge to say to him: I present the oath to you three times. If you swear, then it is fine; otherwise, I will judge against you according to what the plaintiff claims. The ruling is that if the judge presents the oath once to the defendant and he refuses to swear, the judge has the discretion to judge against the defendant. Because in the hadiths above, there is an indication of judgment after one refusal. But since the defendant is not familiar with the matter and may not know the law, it is better that the judge informs him beforehand: I will present the oath to you three times. If you swear, judgment will be in your favor because the plaintiff has no witnesses. And if you refuse to swear all three times, I will judge against you according to what the plaintiff claims. ... It is possible that the defendant does not know the law and after his refusal, judgment will be against him. So he should be told in advance that I will present the oath three times. And after refusal of the oath, judgment will be against you. And three times is for caution, otherwise if he presents the oath once and he... Footnote: (a) The Prophet said: If a woman claims divorce from her husband and brings one upright witness, then her husband is made to swear. If he swears, the witness's testimony is nullified; and if he refuses, his refusal is in the position of a second witness, and the woman's divorce becomes valid. (b) 'Ali considered it necessary for the plaintiff to swear along with the witness.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Da'wa covers two related rulings: (1) the ruling on nukul (the defendant's refusal to take an oath when the plaintiff has no witnesses), and (2) the judge's procedural recommendation to warn the defendant three times before passing judgment. The passage begins by discussing a different scenario (two claimants bringing witnesses and one having possession), then transitions to the main topic. The author explains that if the plaintiff has no witnesses, he may demand that the defendant swear. If the defendant refuses, the judge passes judgment against the defendant, and the plaintiff is not required to swear afterward. The passage also includes a hadith from Amr ibn Shu'ayb showing that nukul is equivalent to a second witness. A significant inter-madhhab dispute is presented: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that after the defendant's refusal, the plaintiff must still swear an oath, citing the practice of 'Ali (a companion). The Hanafi response is that the plaintiff is not required to swear because he already has the benefit of the defendant's refusal, analogous to having a witness; the Shafi'i position is analogous to the case where the plaintiff does have a witness, but here the situation is stronger for the plaintiff. The author notes that the judge should warn the defendant three times to ensure he understands the consequences, though a single refusal suffices for judgment. The passage concludes with procedural advice for the judge.

Key Terms
النكول (al-nukul): The defendant's refusal to take an oath after being asked by the judge when the plaintiff has no witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi court, if the defendant (mudda'a 'alayh) refuses to take the oath (nukul) and the plaintiff has no witnesses, what is the ruling according to the passage?
A) The judge dismisses the case.
B) The judge rules against the defendant without requiring the plaintiff to swear.
C) The judge asks the plaintiff to swear, and then rules in his favor.
D) The judge sends both parties to arbitration.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the defendant's refusal to swear (nukul) is treated as a second witness, enabling the judge to rule against the defendant without requiring the plaintiff to take an oath.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
6 min
Presenting the Oath Three Times and Judgment upon Nukool
Explains the judge's procedure of presenting the oath three times and the effect of refusal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for presenting the oath to a defendant three times and explain that judgment is passed against him upon refusal (nukool), distinguishing the Hanafi view from that of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
The defendant's refusal to swear three times results in judgment against him; the three presentations are a precaution, not a condition.

When a defendant in a claim has no evidence, the judge may present the oath to the defendant. But what if the defendant refuses to swear? This lesson outlines the Hanafi procedure: the judge should present the oath three times as a precaution, and if the defendant refuses all three, judgment is passed against him. We also examine the prophetic proof and the differing view of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the judicial procedure being described: the judge's presentation of the oath to the defendant three times. State the ruling: it is recommended (sunnah) to present three times, but once suffices.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Amr ibn Shu'ayb about a woman claiming divorce. Identify the proof: the hadith equates the defendant's refusal (nukool) to a second witness, leading to judgment.
The hadith is from Ibn Majah, classified as ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Determine how the hadith proves the ruling. The phrase 'nukool is like a second witness' directly shows that refusal triggers judgment without requiring the plaintiff to swear.
Hanafi usul: explicit text (nass) is taken as definitive in meaning.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees: he holds that upon the defendant's refusal, the plaintiff should be sworn. Identify his evidence: an athar from Ali (RA) that the plaintiff swears even with evidence.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school prefers the explicit hadith and also considers that three presentations remove any ignorance, so the defendant is fully warned. The three-time caution is to prevent the defendant from claiming unawareness.
The mufta bihi is that three presentations are recommended but one is sufficient.

كتاب الدعوى
۲۷۴۳ (۱۴) واذا كرر العرض ثلث مرات قضى عليه بالنكول
جبکہ قسم پیش کی مکرر تین مرتبہ تو فیصلہ کیا جائے گا اس کے خلاف انکار کی وجہ سے۔ قاضی نے مدعی علیہ پر تین مرتبہ قسم پیش کی ، مدعی علیہ نے تینوں مرتبہ قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو قاضی اب اس کے خلاف فیصلہ کریں گے۔ تفصیل گزر چکی ہے۔
Book of Claims. It is incumbent upon the judge to say to him (the defendant): 'I present the oath to you three times. If you take the oath, then good; otherwise, I will pass judgment against you according to what the plaintiff claims.' (Hadith from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'If a woman claims divorce from her husband and brings a single just witness to that, her husband is made to take an oath. If he takes the oath, the witness's testimony is invalidated; if he refuses, his refusal is considered as a second witness, and her divorce becomes effective.') (Ibn Majah, Bab al-Rajul Mujadd al-Talaq, p. 292, no. 2038; Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Wikalah, vol. 4, p. 96, no. 4295). In this hadith, refusal to take an oath is considered as a second witness, and judgment will be passed accordingly. Imam al-Shafi'i says: 'Even if the defendant refuses the oath, no judgment is passed; rather, the plaintiff is made to take an oath. He will swear that this thing is his, then judgment will be given in his favor.' There is an athar: 'If the plaintiff produces evidence, he is still made to take an oath, and then judgment is passed.' When he produces a witness, the plaintiff is given the oath. Here, when the defendant refused the oath, doubt increases. So, by analogy, the plaintiff is made to take an oath a fortiori so that it becomes clear that the thing belongs to the plaintiff. (2) The athar is: 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) used to regard the oath along with the evidence.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab man ra' al-hilf ma'a al-bayyinah, vol. 10, p. 441, no. 21248). Due to this athar, the matter rests on the plaintiff. Nukool: Refusal to take an oath. (13) It is appropriate for the judge to say to him: 'I present the oath to you three times. If you take the oath, fine; otherwise, I will pass judgment against you according to what the plaintiff claims.' The difference: Even once, if the judge presents the oath to the defendant and he refuses, the judge has leeway to pass judgment against him. Because in the above hadiths, there is indication that judgment is based on a single refusal. However, since the defendant is not familiar with the matter and may not know the law, it is better that the judge first inform him: 'I will present the oath to you three times. If you take the oath, judgment will be in your favor because the plaintiff has no witness. If you refuse all three times, I will pass judgment against you for what the plaintiff claims.' It is possible that the defendant does not know the law, so he should be told beforehand that after refusal, judgment will be against him. The three times are for caution; otherwise, one presentation is sufficient. And he... Footnote (a): The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'If a woman claims divorce from her husband and brings one just witness, her husband is made to take an oath. If he takes the oath, the witness's testimony is invalidated; if he refuses, his refusal is like a second witness, and the divorce becomes permissible for her.' (b) Sayyiduna Ali regarded the oath of the plaintiff along with the evidence as necessary. (Continued from page 100) (14) And if the presentation is repeated three times, judgment is passed against him due to nukool. When the judge presented the oath three times and the defendant refused all three times, the judge will now pass judgment against him. The detail has passed.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage begins with a ruling: a judge should inform the defendant that he will present the oath three times, and if the defendant refuses, judgment will be against him. The author then provides a hadith from Amr ibn Shu'ayb as a proof. The hadith establishes that in a marriage claim, if a woman brings one witness, the husband is sworn, and if he refuses, his refusal acts as a second witness. The author notes that Imam Shafi'i differs: he says the plaintiff should be sworn instead. The author then mentions an athar from Ali (RA) who held that the plaintiff should be sworn even with evidence. Finally, the author returns to the main ruling and explains the wisdom of presenting the oath three times: to ensure the defendant is aware of the consequences, as he might not know the law. The three-time presentation is a precaution; even once is sufficient. The author then restates the ruling in point (14) that upon three presentations and refusal, judgment is given against the defendant due to nukool.

Key Terms
النكول (al-nukool): Refusal of the defendant to take the oath that is presented to him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of the defendant's refusal (nukool) after the judge presents the oath three times?
A) The plaintiff is sworn.
B) The case is dismissed.
C) Judgment is passed against the defendant.
D) The defendant is given another chance.

Key Takeaway
The defendant's refusal to take the oath after three presentations results in judgment against him, with the three-time caution being a sunnah precaution.

Nukul as Bazl or Iqrar: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Oath Refusal in Marriage Claims
Dispute on refusal of oath in marriage and other claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on the legal effect of nukul in marriage claims and apply their respective rulings.

Core Idea
Nukul is either bazl (relinquishment) or iqrar (admission) — the difference determines whether an oath is administered in marriage.

When a defendant refuses to take an oath after being offered, what does that refusal mean? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, answered this question differently, leading to divergent rulings in several claim types. This lesson examines their disagreement specifically in the context of marriage claims, where the nature of the disputed subject matter — a woman's consent to marriage — makes the choice between bazl and iqrar critical.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position on nukul
Abu Hanifa holds that when a defendant refuses an oath, it is bazl: he gives up the claimed item to avoid swearing, but does not admit the claim. This implies the item is his but he relinquishes it.
This interpretation applies only to cases where the subject matter can be validly relinquished.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's opposing view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider nukul as iqrar: the refusal is an admission of the plaintiff's claim. They see it as equivalent to a second witness.
This view is shared by the three other imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) in most cases.
3
Follow Abu Hanifa's proof
The hadith of Umar: a man ransomed his oath with 1000 dirhams, indicating bazl. Also the hadith of Zuhri: companions ransomed oaths with 10,000 dirhams. These show that refusal can be a transaction rather than admission.
These ahadith are from Bukhari and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb: if a woman claims divorce and brings one witness, the husband is sworn; if he refuses, his nukul is like a second witness. This directly equates nukul with iqrar.
This hadith is in Ibn Majah and Dar Qutni.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf in a marriage claim
If a woman denies marriage without evidence, Abu Hanifa does not swear her (since bazl of herself is invalid). The claim fails. The Sahibayn swear her; if she refuses, the marriage is proven by iqrar.
The practical outcome differs: Abu Hanifa dismisses the case; Sahibayn establish the marriage.

گواہ لائے تو شوہر سے قسم لی جائے گی۔ پس اگر شوہر نے قسم کھائی تو گواہ کی گواہی باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر انکار کر دیا تو اس کا انکار دوسرے گواہ کے درجے میں ہوگا اور طلاق جائز ہو جائے گی۔
The Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 4, p.94: Book of Claims. 2743 (14): If he repeats the offer three times, judgment is passed against him due to nukul. 2744 (15): If the claim is of marriage, the denier is not sworn according to Abu Hanifa. 2745 (16): And no oath is taken in marriage, revocation (رجعة), return in ila', slavery, umm walad, lineage, wala', hudud, and li'an. The explanation follows: When the oath is presented three times and the defendant refuses all three, the judge rules against him. In a marriage claim, the wife is not sworn unless there is evidence; Sahibayn say she is sworn and refusal amounts to admission. Nine cases where Abu Hanifa says no oath, Sahibayn say oath except in hudud and li'an. These branch from two principles: Abu Hanifa's bazl (relinquishment) and Sahibayn's iqrar (admission). Bazl: the defendant says 'the thing is mine but I give it to you rather than swear.' Evidence: hadith of Huzayl and Umar's judgment where a man ransomed his oath for 1000 dirhams. Another hadith: a man ransomed his oath for 10,000 dirhams. Sahibayn say refusal is admission, supported by hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb: if a woman claims divorce and brings one witness, the husband is sworn; if he refuses, his nukul is like a second witness. Application to marriage: Abu Hanifa says wife cannot give herself as bazl without marriage, so no oath; Sahibayn say refusal is admission and marriage is proven.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh al-Thamiri discusses the rulings on a defendant's refusal to take an oath (nukul) and its consequences. The author presents a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). According to Abu Hanifa, when a defendant is offered an oath three times and refuses each time, the judge rules against him. However, in certain types of claims—namely marriage, revocation of divorce, return from ila', slavery, umm walad, lineage, wala', hudud, and li'an—the defendant is not to be sworn at all. The Sahibayn disagree, holding that an oath should be administered in all these cases except hudud and li'an. The underlying difference is in the interpretation of nukul: Abu Hanifa considers it as bazl (relinquishment of the claim), where the defendant gives up the disputed item to avoid swearing, while the Sahibayn consider it as iqrar (admission) of the plaintiff's claim. The author cites several hadith to support each view. The practical consequence: in a marriage claim where the woman denies the marriage, Abu Hanifa does not swear her because if she refuses, her bazl would imply giving herself in marriage without a contract, which is invalid; thus the marriage cannot be proven without evidence. The Sahibayn, however, would swear her, and her refusal would be taken as admission, establishing the marriage.

Key Terms
النكول (al-nukul): Refusal of the defendant to take the oath tendered by the judge after the plaintiff has no evidence.
البذل (al-bazl): The defendant's voluntary relinquishment of the disputed property to avoid swearing, implying the item is his but he gifts it.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Admission of the plaintiff's claim, which results from the defendant's refusal to swear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is a defendant not sworn in a claim of marriage?
A) Because marriage claims require two witnesses and no oath can substitute.
B) Because the defendant's nukul would be bazl, and a woman cannot give herself in marriage through bazl.
C) Because the judge must always decide in favor of the plaintiff in marriage claims.
D) Because the defendant's nukul is automatically considered iqrar.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the legal effect of refusing an oath depends on the nature of the claim—property claims allow bazl, but personal status claims like marriage require iqrar, leading to different rulings between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Nukul: Bazzl or Iqrar?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nukul with proofs and application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on nukul (Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn) and apply them to determine whether an oath is administered in claims involving bodily rights versus property.

Core Idea
Nukul is interpreted as offering the object (bazzl) by Abu Hanifa and as admission (iqrar) by the Sahibayn—this determines oath administration in personal status cases.

This passage presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal effect of nukul (refusal to take an oath). Imam Abu Hanifa views nukul as an implicit offer to surrender the disputed item (bazzl), which is only valid for property and not for bodily rights. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) view nukul as an admission (iqrar), valid in all claims. This disagreement leads to practical differences in how judges handle oaths in marriage, revocable divorce, and similar matters. The passage cites athar from Umar and al-Zuhri supporting bazzl, and a hadith from Ibn Majah supporting iqrar, then applies the two principles to several cases.

Guided Path
1
State the two Hanafi positions on nukul
Identify that Abu Hanifa considers nukul as bazzl (offering the object) while the Sahibayn consider it as iqrar (admission). Note that this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
The Sahibayn's view is also held by the other three Sunni schools.
2
Locate the proofs for each position
Find the athar from Umar and al-Zuhri that show people ransoming themselves from oaths by giving money – this supports bazzl. Find the hadith from Ibn Majah where the Prophet equates nukul to a second witness – this supports iqrar.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but used as evidence.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In claims involving bodily acts (nisah, marriage, raj'ah, ila'), Abu Hanifa does not administer the oath because nukul would imply bazzl which is invalid for the body. The Sahibayn administer the oath because nukul constitutes admission. In property claims, both agree that nukul is effective.
The key distinction is whether the subject matter is property or a personal right.
4
Apply the positions to specific cases
Walk through the nikah and raj'ah examples given in the text. For each, determine whether an oath is administered according to each imam.
For nikah: Abu Hanifa says no oath; Sahibayn say yes oath.

والولاء والحدود واللعان وقالا يُستحلف في ذلك كله الا في الحدود واللعان . ۶۸۹۹) اس اثر میں حضرت عمر نے فرمایا کہ نکال باہر کرنے پر پچاس آدمی سے قسم لیں، انچاس آدمیوں سے قسم لی ۔ پھر ایک آدمی شام سے آیا اس سے قسم کھانے کے لئے کہا تو اس نے قسم نہیں کھائی اور قسم نہ کھانے کے فدیہ میں ایک ہزار درہم دیئے اس کو بذل کہتے ہیں۔ یعنی چیز تو میری ہی ہے لیکن چلو تم کو دے دیتا ہوں اور قسم نہیں کھاتا ہوں (۲) دوسرے اثر میں ہے۔ مسئل الزهرى عن الرجل يقع عليه اليمين فيريد ان يفتدى يمينه قال قد كان يفعل قد افتدى عبيد السهام في امارة مروان و اصحاب رسول الله الا الله بالمدينة كثير افتدى يـمـيـنـه بعشرة آلاف (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب من يجب عليه التكفير ج ثامن ص ۵۰۲ نمبر ۱۲۰۵۴ ردار قطنی ، کتاب فی الاضحية والاحکام ج رابع ص ۱۵۸ نمبر۴۵۵۰) اس اثر میں تذکرہ ہے کہ اصحاب رسول قسم کے بدلے دس ہزار درہم کا فدیہ دیتے تھے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قسم سے انکار کرنا بذل ہے اور فدیہ ہے۔ نانه صاحبین اور ائمہ ثلاثہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قسم کھانے سے انکار کرنا اقرار کرنا ہے، گویا کہ دبے زبان میں اقرار کر رہا ہے کہ یہ چیز حقیقت میں اور سے کہ میں کر رہا ہے یہ چیز آپ ہی کی ہے اس لئے میں قسم نہیں کھاتا ہوں۔ اور جب آپ کی ہے تو آپ کو قاضی دے دیں۔
حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن عمرو بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده عن النبي الله قال اذا ادعت المرأة طلاق زوجها فجاءت على ذلك بشاهد عدل استحلف زوجها فان حلف بطلت شهادة الشاهد وان نكل فنكوله بمنزلة شاهد آخر وجاز طلاقه (ب) (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب الرجل بجد الطلاق ص۲۹۲ نمبر ۲۰۳۸ ردار قطنی ، کتاب الوکاله ج رابع ص ۹۶ نمبر ۴۲۹۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کا قسم سے انکار کرنا اقرار کرنے کے درجے میں ہے اور دوسری گواہی کی درجے میں ہے۔ ان دونوں اصولوں کو سامنے رکھ کر نو مسائل کا حل اس طرح ہے۔
[1] نکاح : نکاح کی صورت یہ ہے کہ مثلا شو ہر دعوی کرے کہ فلاں عورت سے میری شادی ہوئی ہے اور عورت اس کا انکار کرتی ہے۔ اور شوہر کے پاس بعینہ نہیں ہے۔ اب عورت کو قسم کھلائیں۔ اور اس نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک انکار کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ نکاح تو نہیں ہوا ہے لیکن چلو میری شرمگاہ تم استعمال کرو۔ اور شرعی اعتبار سے ایسا نہیں کر سکتی کہ بغیر نکاح کے اپنے آپ کو بذل کے طور پر استعمال کرنے دے۔ اس لئے عورت کو قسم ہی نہیں دیں گے بلکہ بعینہ نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے نکاح ثابت ہی نہیں کریں گے۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک قسم سے انکار کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ میں اقرار کرتی ہوں کہ شوہر کی بات صحیح ہے اور نکاح ہوا ہے۔ اور جب اقرار کر لیا تو نکاح ہوا ہے تو اپنے آپ کو استعمال کرنے بھی دے گی۔ اس لئے صاحبین کے نزدیک مدعی علیہا کو قسم کھلائیں گے۔ (۲) رجعت : رجعت کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ شوہر نے بیوی کو طلاق رجعی دی۔ عدت گزر جانے کے بعد شوہر دعوی کرتا ہے کہ میں نے عدت کے اندر رجعت کر لی تھی۔ اور عورت انکار کرتی ہے کہ رجعت نہیں کی تھی ۔ شوہر کے پاس بینہ نہیں ہے۔ اب امام صاحب کے نزدیک عورت کو قسم نہیں کھلا ئیں گے بلکہ بغیر قسم کے ہی فیصلہ کر دیں گے کہ رجعت نہیں ہوئی تھی۔ اگر قسم کھلائیں اور عورت قسم کھانے سے انکار کر جائے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ رجعت تو نہیں ہوئی ہے اور نہ میں تمہاری بیوی ہوں۔ لیکن چلو بذل کے طور پر تم مجھے استعمال کرتے رہو۔ اور رجعت نہ ہو تو بذل کے طور پر اور فدیہ کے طور پر اپنے آپ کو استعمال کرنے نہیں دے سکتی ۔ اس لئے قسم ہی نہیں لی جائے گی۔ اگر جسم کے بجائے مال ہوتا تو بذل کے طور پر اس کو استعمال کرنے دینا جائز ہے اس لئے وہاں قسم کھلائی جائے گی۔ ای صاحبین کے نزدیک قسم سے انکار کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ میں دبے زبان اقرار کرتی ہوں کہ شوہر نے عدت میں رجعت کی تھی اور میں اس کی بیوی ہوں۔ اس لئے صاحبین کے نزدیک رجعت میں عورت سے قسم لی جائے گی۔ نوٹ اگر عدت کے اندر شوہر نے کہا کہ میں نے رجعت کی ہے اور عورت نے انکار کیا تو اگر چہ اس سے پہلے رجعت نہیں ہوئی ہے لیکن ابھی شوہر کے کہنے سے ہی رجعت ہو جائے گی۔ (۳) ایلاء میں فی : شوہر نے بیوی سے کہا کہ میں چار ماہ تک تمہارے قریب نہیں جاؤں گا اس کو ایلاء کہتے ہیں۔ اب اگر چار ماہ کے اندر بیوی کے پاس نہیں گیا تو بیوی کو طلاق بائنہ واقع ہوگی اور نکاح ختم ہو جائے گا۔ چار ماہ کے اندر بیوی کے پاس نہ جانے کوئی کہتے ہیں۔ عدت گزر جانے کے بعد شوہر کہتا ہے کہ میں نے چار ماہ کے اندرفی کی تھی۔ بیوی انکار کرتی ہے۔ شوہر کے پاس بینہ نہیں ہے تو بیوی کو اس بارے میں قسم نہیں کھلائیں گے۔ کیونکہ قسم سے انکار کرنے کا معنی بدل ہوگا ۔ یعنی میں تمہاری بیوی تو نہیں ہوں کیونکہ چار ماہ کے اندر فی نہیں کی لیکن چلو اپنے آپ کو استعمال کرنے دیتی ہوں ۔ چونکہ نکاح کے بغیر اپنے آپ کو استعمال کرنے نہیں دے سکتی اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک ذرت پر تم نہیں ہوگی۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک قسم سے انکار کا مطلب اقرار ہے۔ یعنی دبے زبان اقرار کر رہی ہے کہ واقعی آپ نے چار ماہ کے اندرفی کی تھی اور میں آپ کی بیوی ہوں اس لئے ان کے نزدیک ایلاء کے فی میں قسم کھلائیں گے۔
اگر چار ماہ کے اندر شوہر کہے کہ میں نے فی کی ہے تو پہلے فی نہیں ہوئی البتہ ابھی اس کہنے سے فی ہو جائے گی۔
اصول یہ مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ نکاح برقرار ر ہے بغیر اپنے آپ کو سپرد نہیں کر سکتی جسم مال نہیں ہے کہ بذل کر دے۔ (۴) الرق : غلام ہونے یا غلام بننے کا دعوی۔ ایک آدمی مجہول الحال ہے۔ اس کے بارے میں ایک آدمی کہتا ہے کہ یہ میر الغلام ہے اور مجہول الحال آدمی اس کا انکار کرتا ہے۔ دعوی کرنے والے کے پاس بینہ نہیں ہے۔ اب غلام سے قسم کھلا ئیں اور وہ قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ میں تمہارا غلام تو نہیں ہوں لیکن چلو اپنے آپ کو تمہاری غلامیت میں دے دیتا ہوں۔ لیکن کوئی بھی
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Volume 4, page 95. Book of Claims and Oaths and Hudud and Li'an. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is made to swear in all of that except in hudud and li'an. 6899. In this Athar, Hadrat Umar said: For expelling outside, take oaths from fifty men, take oaths from ninety-nine men. Then a man came from Syria, he (Umar) asked him to take an oath, but he did not take an oath and gave one thousand dirhams as compensation for not taking an oath. This is called bazzl: that is, the thing is mine, but come I give it to you and I do not take an oath. (2) In another Athar: Al-Zuhri was asked about a man upon whom an oath falls and he wants to ransom his oath. He said: It used to be done. 'Ubayd al-Siham ransomed during the governorship of Marwan, and the Companions of the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and give him peace) were many in Medina; he ransomed his oath for ten thousand (dirhams). (Source: Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab man yajibu alayhi al-takfir, vol. 8, p. 502, no. 12054; Dar Qutni, Kitab fi al-Udhiyah wa al-Ahkam, vol. 4, p. 158, no. 4550) In this Athar, it is mentioned that the Companions of the Messenger used to give ransom for the oath. From this it is known that refusal to take an oath is bazzl and ransom. Nay, the Two Companions (Sahibayn) and the Three Imams say that refusal to take an oath is admission (iqrar), as if he is admitting in a low voice that this thing is in reality yours, that is why I am not taking an oath. And when it is yours, then give it to the judge. The hadith indicates this: From Amr ibn Shu'ayb, from his father, from his grandfather, from the Prophet (may Allah bless him and give him peace): If a woman claims divorce from her husband and brings one just witness for that, then her husband is made to take an oath. If he takes an oath, the witness's testimony is invalidated. If he refuses (nukul), then his refusal is like another witness, and his divorce is valid. (Ibn Majah, Bab al-Rajul yajid al-talaq, p. 292, no. 2038; Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Wikalah, vol. 4, p. 96, no. 4295) This hadith indicates that the defendant's refusal to take an oath is in the position of admission and in the position of a second witness. Keeping these two principles in view, the solution of nine issues is as follows: [1] Nikah: The case of marriage: For example, a husband claims that he married a certain woman, and the woman denies it. The husband has no evidence. The woman is asked to take an oath. If she refuses, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the meaning of refusal is that the marriage did not occur, but come, you may use my private part. And from a Shariah perspective, she cannot do that, i.e., allow herself to be used as bazzl without marriage. Therefore, she will not be asked to take an oath at all; rather, due to lack of evidence, the marriage will not be established. According to the Sahibayn, the meaning of refusal is that I admit that the husband is correct and the marriage occurred. And when she admits the marriage, she will also allow herself to be used. Therefore, according to the Sahibayn, the defendant woman will be asked to take an oath. (2) Raj'ah: The case of raj'ah: The husband gave his wife a revocable divorce. After the iddah passed, the husband claims that he had taken her back (raj'ah) during the iddah. The woman denies that he took her back. The husband has no evidence. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, she will not be asked to take an oath; rather, the decision will be made without an oath that raj'ah did not occur. If she were asked to take an oath and she refused, the meaning would be: raj'ah did not occur and I am not your wife, but come, you may use me as bazzl. And if raj'ah did not occur, she cannot allow herself to be used as bazzl or ransom. Therefore, the oath is not taken from her. If it were property instead of the body, then allowing its use as bazzl would be permissible, so the oath would be taken there. According to the Sahibayn, the meaning of refusal is that I admit in a low voice that the husband took me back during the iddah and I am his wife. Therefore, according to them, in the case of raj'ah, the woman is asked to take an oath. Note: If during the iddah the husband says 'I took her back' and the woman denies, then even if raj'ah had not occurred before, it will occur by his statement now. (3) Ila' and Fi'ah: The husband said to his wife: 'I will not go near you for four months.' This is called ila'. If he does not go to her within four months, a ba'in divorce occurs and the marriage ends. 'Going to her within four months' is called fi'ah. After the iddah passes, the husband says: 'I did fi'ah within four months.' The wife denies. The husband has no evidence. The wife will not be asked to take an oath in this matter, because the meaning of refusal to take an oath is bazzl: that is, I am not your wife because I did not do fi'ah within four months, but come, I let you use me. Since she cannot allow herself to be used without marriage, therefore according to the Hanafis, she will not be (made to do anything?). According to the Sahibayn, the meaning of refusal is admission: that is, in a low voice she admits that you actually did fi'ah within four months and I am your wife. Therefore, according to them, in fi'ah of ila', the oath will be taken from her. If within four months the husband says 'I did fi'ah', even if fi'ah had not occurred before, now by this saying it will occur. Principle: These issues are based on the principle that the marriage remains intact; she cannot surrender herself without a proper basis; the body is not property to be given as bazzl. (4) Al-Riqq: The claim of being a slave or becoming a slave. A man whose status is unknown (majhul al-hal). About him, a man says: 'This is my slave,' and the unknown man denies. The claimant has no evidence. Now the slave is asked to take an oath. If he refuses, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the meaning will be: 'I am not your slave, but come, I give myself into your slavery.' But no one...
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the legal effect of nukul (refusal to take an oath) in claims. The author first presents two historical effects (athar) from Sayyiduna Umar and al-Zuhri that show the concept of bazzl (ransoming oneself from an oath by giving the disputed property). According to these effects, when a person refuses to swear, they may pay a ransom (fidyah) to avoid the oath, implying that the object is theirs but they offer it. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa: nukul is akin to bazzl—the person is effectively saying 'I won't swear, but here, take the thing.' However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and the three Imams (presumably the other madhhab founders) hold that nukul is equivalent to iqrar (admission). The person's refusal is a tacit acknowledgment that the claim is true, because if the claim were false, they would swear to rebut it. The text then cites a hadith from Ibn Majah where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled that if a man refuses to swear in a divorce claim, his refusal is like a second witness, making the divorce valid. The author then applies these two principles to nine issues (though only four are discussed in this window). The first issue is nikah: If a husband claims marriage and the woman refuses to swear, Abu Hanifa says her refusal is bazzl—she offers herself but this is invalid because the body is not property. Hence, the oath is not administered and the marriage is not proven. The Sahibayn say her refusal is admission, so the oath is administered. The second issue is raj'ah: similar reasoning; the body cannot be bazzl, so Abu Hanifa does not administer the oath, while the Sahibayn do. The third issue is ila' and fi'ah: again, the body is not bazzl, so Abu Hanifa does not administer the oath; the Sahibayn do. The fourth issue is slavery (riqq): Abu Hanifa considers the slave's refusal as bazzl (offering himself into slavery), which is valid because a slave is property, so the oath is administered; however, the text is cut off before completing the Sahibayn's view. The underlying principle is that the body (for free persons) is not subject to bazzl, while property is.

Key Terms
نكول (nukul): Refusal to take an oath when it is required in a legal claim.
بذل (bazzl): Offering the disputed property or object as ransom to avoid taking an oath, implying that the object is yours but you give it up rather than swear.
اقرار (iqrar): Admission or confession. In this context, the Sahibayn view that not swearing amounts to admitting the claim against oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), what is the legal effect of nukul (refusal to take an oath) in a claim?
A) It is equivalent to bazzl (offering the object).
B) It is equivalent to iqrar (admission).
C) It has no legal effect.
D) It invalidates the claim entirely.

Key Takeaway
Nukul (refusal to swear) is interpreted either as bazzl (Abu Hanifa) or iqrar (Sahibayn), with the key practical difference being that the latter allows oath administration in all claims, while the former restricts it to property cases.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
15 min
The Principle of Administering Oaths in Claims Involving the Body
Intra-Hanafi dispute on oath in bodily claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi disagreement on the interpretation of a defendant's refusal to take an oath in bodily claims, and apply the principle to at least three of the eight cases presented.

Core Idea
A defendant's refusal to swear an oath in bodily claims is not an admission because the body cannot be given away.

In Hanafi jurisprudence, when a plaintiff lacks evidence, the defendant may be required to take an oath. But what if the defendant refuses? This passage from Sharh al-Thamiri reveals a critical disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his disciples, the Sahibayn, over the legal significance of such refusal in cases involving the body. The resolution hinges on the nature of the body as non-property (mal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
A plaintiff makes a claim involving a bodily right (e.g., marriage, slavery) without witnesses. The defendant is asked to take an oath but refuses. What does this refusal mean legally?
This is the nukul scenario.
2
Contrast the two Hanafi interpretations
Imam Abu Hanifa interprets refusal as bazl (mere offer to submit without admission), which is invalid for the body. The Sahibayn interpret it as iqrar bi al-dabin (implicit admission), which is valid.
The key difference: bazl is ineffective, iqrar is effective.
3
Apply to the nikah case
A man claims marriage, woman denies, no witnesses. If she refuses the oath, Abu Hanifa says no ruling against her because her refusal would mean she is offering herself without marriage (invalid). Sahibayn say refusal implies admission, so oath is administered.
This is the first sub-case.
4
Extend to other bodily claims
The same reasoning applies to ruj'ah, ila', riq, istilad, nasab, wala', and hudud. In each, the dispute is whether refusal implies admission or mere offer.
The principle is uniform across all cases.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the claim is rejected without oath; under Sahibayn, the claim is upheld if the defendant refuses the oath.
This determines who wins the case.

نکاح ہوا ہے تو اپنے آپ کو استعمال کرنے بھی دے گی۔ اس لئے صاحبین کے نزدیک مدعی علیہا کو قسم کھلائیں گے۔ (۲) رجعت : رجعت کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ شوہر نے بیوی کو طلاق رجعی دی۔ عدت گزر جانے کے بعد شوہر دعوی کرتا ہے کہ میں نے عدت کے اندر رجعت کر لی تھی۔ اور عورت انکار کرتی ہے کہ رجعت نہیں کی تھی ۔ شوہر کے پاس بینہ نہیں ہے۔ اب امام صاحب کے نزدیک عورت کو قسم نہیں کھلا ئیں گے بلکہ بغیر قسم کے ہی فیصلہ کر دیں گے کہ رجعت نہیں ہوئی تھی۔ اگر قسم کھلائیں اور عورت قسم کھانے سے انکار کر جائے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ رجعت تو نہیں ہوئی ہے اور نہ میں تمہاری بیوی ہوں۔ لیکن چلو بذل کے طور پر تم مجھے استعمال کرتے رہو۔ اور رجعت نہ ہو تو بذل کے طور پر اور فدیہ کے طور پر اپنے آپ کو استعمال کرنے نہیں دے سکتی ۔ اس لئے قسم ہی نہیں لی جائے گی۔ اگر جسم کے بجائے مال ہوتا تو بذل کے طور پر اس کو استعمال کرنے دینا جائز ہے اس لئے وہاں قسم کھلائی جائے گی۔ ای صاحبین کے نزدیک قسم سے انکار کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ میں دبے زبان اقرار کرتی ہوں کہ شوہر نے عدت میں رجعت کی تھی اور میں اس کی بیوی ہوں۔ اس لئے صاحبین کے نزدیک رجعت میں عورت سے قسم لی جائے گی۔ نوٹ اگر عدت کے اندر شوہر نے کہا کہ میں نے رجعت کی ہے اور عورت نے انکار کیا تو اگر چہ اس سے پہلے رجعت نہیں ہوئی ہے لیکن ابھی شوہر کے کہنے سے ہی رجعت ہو جائے گی۔ (۳) ایلاء میں فی : شوہر نے بیوی سے کہا کہ میں چار ماہ تک تمہارے قریب نہیں جاؤں گا اس کو ایلاء کہتے ہیں۔ اب اگر چار ماہ کے اندر بیوی کے پاس نہیں گیا تو بیوی کو طلاق بائنہ واقع ہوگی اور نکاح ختم ہو جائے گا۔ چار ماہ کے اندر بیوی کے پاس نہ جانے کوئی کہتے ہیں۔ عدت گزر جانے کے بعد شوہر کہتا ہے کہ میں نے چار ماہ کے اندرفی کی تھی۔ بیوی انکار کرتی ہے۔ شوہر کے پاس بینہ نہیں ہے تو بیوی کو اس بارے میں قسم نہیں کھلائیں گے۔ کیونکہ قسم سے انکار کرنے کا معنی بدل ہوگا ۔ یعنی میں تمہاری بیوی تو نہیں ہوں کیونکہ چار ماہ کے اندر فی نہیں کی لیکن چلو اپنے آپ کو استعمال کرنے دیتی ہوں ۔ چونکہ نکاح کے بغیر اپنے آپ کو استعمال کرنے نہیں دے سکتی اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک ذرت پر تم نہیں ہوگی۔
ن صاحبین کے نزدیک قسم سے انکار کا مطلب اقرار ہے۔ یعنی دبے زبان اقرار کر رہی ہے کہ واقعی آپ نے چار ماہ کے اندرفی کی تھی اور میں آپ کی بیوی ہوں اس لئے ان کے نزدیک ایلاء کے فی میں قسم کھلائیں گے۔
اگر چار ماہ کے اندر شوہر کہے کہ میں نے فی کی ہے تو پہلے فی نہیں ہوئی البتہ ابھی اس کہنے سے فی ہو جائے گی۔
اصول یہ مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ نکاح برقرار ر ہے بغیر اپنے آپ کو سپرد نہیں کر سکتی جسم مال نہیں ہے کہ بذل کر دے۔ (۳) الرق : غلام ہونے یا غلام بننے کا دعوی۔ ایک آدمی مجہول الحال ہے۔ اس کے بارے میں ایک آدمی کہتا ہے کہ یہ میر الغلام ہے اور مجہول الحال آدمی اس کا انکار کرتا ہے۔ دعوی کرنے والے کے پاس بینہ نہیں ہے۔ اب غلام سے قسم کھلا ئیں اور وہ قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ میں تمہارا غلام تو نہیں ہوں لیکن چلو اپنے آپ کو تمہاری غلامیت میں دے دیتا ہوں۔ لیکن کوئی بھی

آدمی اپنے آپ کو غلام نہیں بنا سکتا، جسم مال نہیں ہے کہ بذل کر دے۔ اس لئے امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک غلام کو تم نہیں دے سکتا۔ فائدہ صاحبین کے نزدیک قسم کھانے سے انکار کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ دبے زبان اقرار کرتا ہوں کہ میں اس کا غلام ہوں اور پہلے سے غلام ہو تو اس
کا اقرار کر سکتا ہے۔
[۵] الاستيلاد : استیلاد کی صورت یہ ہے کہ شوہر کہے کہ یہ میرا بیٹا ہے۔ کیونکہ میں نے اس کو تم سے پیدا کیا ہے۔ اور عورت انکار کرے۔ شوہر کے پاس بینہ نہ ہو۔ اب عورت کو قسم دے اور وہ قسم کھانے سے انکار کرے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک بذل ہوگا یعنی یہ بچہ آپ کا تو نہیں ہے لیکن چلو آپ سے نسب ثابت کر دیتی ہوں۔ اور نسب ثابت کرنے کا مسئلہ ایسا نہیں ہے کہ بچہ اس کا نہ بھی ہو پھر بھی اس سے نسب ثابت کر دے۔ اس لئے عورت سے استیلاد کے سلسلے میں قسم نہیں کھلائی جائے گی۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ میں دبے زبان سے اقرار کرتی ہوں کہ بچہ آپ کا ہی ہے۔ جب بچہ حقیقت میں شوہر کا ہو تو اس سے نسب ثابت کرنے میں کائی حرج نہیں ہے۔
[۲] النسب : ایک آدمی دعوی کرے کہ یہ آدمی میرالڑکا ہے اور میں اس کا باپ ہوں۔ اور وہ اس کا انکار کرے اور دعوی کرنے والے کے پاس گواہ نہ ہو تو اس آدمی کو قسم نہیں کھلائیں گے، کیونکہ قسم سے انکار کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ میں تمہارا بیٹا تو نہیں ہوں لیکن چلو بیٹا بن جاتا ہوں۔ اور بیٹا نہ ہو اور بذل کے طور پر نسب ثابت کر دے تو جائز نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں منع فرمایا ہے۔ اس لئے نسب کے سلسلے میں لڑکے کو ختم نہیں دی جائے گی۔
صاحبین کے نزدیک قسم سے انکار کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ دبے زبان اقرار کر رہا ہے کہ حقیقت میں میں آپ کا بیٹا ہوں اس لئے لڑکے سے
قسم لے سکتا ہے۔ [۷] الولاء : آزاد کردہ غلام مر جائے اور اس کا کوئی وارث نہ ہوتو وہ مال آزاد کرنے والے آقا کو ملتا ہے اس مال کو ولاء کہتے ہیں۔ یہاں ولاء کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی دوسرے آدمی پر دعوی کرے کہ یہ میرا آزاد کردہ غلام ہے اور اس کا ولاء مجھے ملے گا۔ وہ اس کو انکار کرے کہ میں اس کا آزاد کردہ غلام نہیں ہوں اور نہ میری ولاء اس کو ملے گی۔ دعوی کرنے والے کے پاس بینہ نہیں ہے۔ اب مدعی علیہ کو تم کھلائیں اور وہ قتسم کھانے سے انکار کر جائے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ میں تمہارا آزاد کردہ غلام تو نہیں ہوں لیکن چلو بن جاتا ہوں ۔ تو شرعی اعتبار سے ایسا نہیں کر سکتا کیونکہ آزاد جان کو غلام بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے مدعی علیہ کو ولاء کی قسم بھی نہیں کھلا سکتا۔
صاحبین کے نزدیک قسم سے انکار کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ دبے زبان اس کا اقرار کرتا ہوں کہ میں اس کا آزاد کردہ غلام ہوں اور میری ولاء
ان کو ملنی چاہئے ۔ اور حقیقت میں آزاد کردہ غلام ہو تو قسم دی جاسکتی ہے۔ [۸] الحدود : کوئی آدمی کسی آدمی پر دعوی کرے کہ میرا تمہارے اوپر حد قذف ہے۔ اور دوسرا آدمی اس کا انکار کرے اور دعوی کرنے والے کے پاس گواہی نہیں ہے تو مدعی علیہ کو تم نہیں کھلوائیں گے۔ کیونکہ قسم کھانے سے انکار کر جائے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ مجھ پر آپ کا حد قذف تو نہیں ہے لیکن چلو اسی کوڑے مارلیں۔ ایسا نہیں کر سکتا کیونکہ جسم ایسی چیز نہیں ہے جس کو بذل کے طور پر کوڑے اور حد لگانے کے لئے پیش کیا
The Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 4, page 96, Book of Claims. (1) Nikah: ... (2) Ruj'ah: ... (3) Ila': ... (4) Riq: ... (5) Istilad: ... (6) Nasab: ... (7) Wala': ... (8) Hudud: ... (Full text in Urdu above.)
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh al-Thamiri is an intra-Hanafi dispute, explaining the principle for when a defendant should be made to take an oath in claims involving the body. The core issue is the legal interpretation of the defendant's refusal (nukul) to take the oath. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, refusal should be interpreted as a mere offer (bazl) to allow the claim without actual admission. Since a free person's body is not property and cannot be given away or subjected to bodily rights without a valid marriage or ownership, such an offer is legally ineffective. Therefore, in cases involving marriage, revocation of divorce, waiver of sexual rights (ila'), slavery, paternity, lineage, patronage, and fixed punishments, Imam Abu Hanifa does not administer the oath to the defendant. In contrast, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) interpret refusal as an implicit admission (iqrar bi al-dabin) of the claim. Hence, they administer the oath in these cases. The passage then applies this principle to eight specific scenarios: (1) nikah claim, (2) ruj'ah claim, (3) ila' claim, (4) slavery claim, (5) istilad (claim of paternity from a wife), (6) nasab (lineage claim from a child), (7) wala' (patronage claim), and (8) hadd al-qadhf (slander punishment claim). In each sub-case, the author reiterates the same difference of opinion. Note: For nikah, the imam mentioned is Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn require an oath from the woman. For ruj'ah, Abu Hanifa gives no oath because the wife cannot offer herself as a gift without marriage; Sahibayn give oath as refusal implies admission. For ila', similar reasoning. For slavery, Abu Hanifa says one cannot make himself a slave; Sahibayn say refusal implies he is a slave. For istilad, Abu Hanifa says the wife cannot establish lineage for a child that is not the husband's; Sahibayn say refusal implies the child is his. For nasab, Abu Hanifa cites a hadith forbidding claiming a false lineage; Sahibayn say refusal implies truth. For wala', Abu Hanifa says one cannot accept patronage by offer; Sahibayn say refusal implies he is the freed slave. For hudud, Abu Hanifa says one cannot submit to a hadd punishment voluntarily; Sahibayn would administer oath. The passage ends with the author noting that for each case, if the defendant refuses, the claim is decided against them only according to Sahibayn; according to Abu Hanifa, no oath is administered and the claim is rejected without oath.

Key Terms
بذل (bazl): A mere offer or gifting without legal consideration; in this context, offering oneself (one's body) for something without a valid legal basis.
اقرار بدبے زبان (iqrar bi al-dabin): Implicit admission; when a party refuses an oath but does not explicitly admit, their refusal is taken as an admission of the claim.
نکول (nukul): Refusal to take an oath when required. In this passage, nukul is the act of the defendant refusing the oath after the plaintiff lacks evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is the oath not administered to a woman in a claim of marriage (nikah) when the plaintiff has no evidence?
A) Because the woman's testimony is not accepted.
B) Because if she refuses the oath, it would imply bazl (offering herself) which is invalid.
C) Because marriage claims require four witnesses.
D) Because the woman is always believed without oath.

Key Takeaway
In bodily claims, refusal to swear an oath does not equal admission because the body cannot be offered as property; this intra-Hanafi dispute affects eight different case types.
